  "file_text": "# Kubernetes API Server Library: Architecture and Extension Guide\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies](#1-subsystem-purpose-boundaries-and-dependencies)\n2. [Key Components](#2-key-components)\n3. [End-to-End Request Flow](#3-end-to-end-request-flow)\n4. [Failure Modes and Tradeoffs](#4-failure-modes-and-tradeoffs)\n5. [Extension Points](#5-extension-points)\n6. [Operational Implications](#6-operational-implications)\n7. [File Map](#7-file-map)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\n`k8s.io/apiserver` is the generic API server framework that all Kubernetes control-plane API servers are built on. It provides the complete machinery for serving a versioned, authenticated, authorized, admission-controlled, and storage-backed HTTP API that follows Kubernetes API conventions. The library is not a standalone binary; it is a reusable foundation that concrete servers compose by supplying resource-specific storage implementations and configuration.\n\nThree production servers build directly on this library:\n\n- **kube-apiserver** (`cmd/kube-apiserver`) \u2014 the main Kubernetes API server, which registers the core and named API groups.\n- **kube-aggregator** (`staging/src/k8s.io/kube-aggregator`) \u2014 the aggregation layer that proxies requests to extension API servers.\n- **apiextensions-apiserver** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver`) \u2014 the CRD server.\n\nAll three are composed into a single process via a delegation chain assembled in `cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go:CreateServerChain`.\n\n### Boundaries\n\nThe library owns:\n\n- TLS termination and HTTP/2 serving (`pkg/server/secure_serving.go`)\n- The filter chain (authentication, authorization, admission, rate limiting, audit, tracing)\n- Route registration and content negotiation (`pkg/endpoints/`)\n- The generic registry (`pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go`) that implements CRUD semantics on top of a pluggable storage backend\n- The watch cache (`pkg/storage/cacher/`) that serves Watch and List from memory\n- The etcd3 storage backend (`pkg/storage/etcd3/`)\n- Lifecycle management: startup hooks, graceful shutdown signals, health/readiness endpoints\n\nThe library does **not** own:\n\n- The schema of any specific Kubernetes resource (those live in `k8s.io/api` and `k8s.io/kubernetes/pkg/apis/`)\n- Admission plugin logic (plugins register themselves; the library provides the chain and interfaces)\n- Controller logic (controllers run as post-start hooks or separate processes)\n- The aggregation proxy logic (owned by kube-aggregator)\n\n### Dependencies\n\n| Dependency | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `k8s.io/apimachinery` | Runtime object model, scheme, codec, field selectors, resource version parsing |\n| `k8s.io/api` | Concrete API types used by built-in admission and flow control |\n| `k8s.io/client-go` | Informers and listers used by the APF controller and admission webhooks |\n| `go.etcd.io/etcd/client/v3` | etcd3 wire protocol (wrapped by `pkg/storage/etcd3/`) |\n| `github.com/emicklei/go-restful/v3` | Route registration for API groups |\n| `go.opentelemetry.io/otel` | Distributed tracing spans |\n| `k8s.io/component-base/tracing` | Tracing provider abstraction |\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components\n\n### 2.1 Config and CompletedConfig\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go`\n\n`Config` is the central configuration struct for a `GenericAPIServer`. It is populated by option structs (e.g., `options.ServerRunOptions`) and then finalized by calling `Complete()`, which returns a `CompletedConfig`. The `Complete()` call fills in defaults and validates mutual constraints; a `CompletedConfig` is the only type that can call `New()` to produce a server.\n\nKey fields and their behavioral implications:\n\n- **`SecureServing *SecureServingInfo`** \u2014 TLS configuration, certificate sources, and HTTP/2 settings. If `DisableHTTP2` is false and `GoawayChance > 0`, the handler chain inserts `WithProbabilisticGoaway` to periodically send HTTP/2 GOAWAY frames, nudging clients to reconnect and rebalance across replicas.\n- **`Authentication AuthenticationInfo`** \u2014 holds the `Authenticator` chain and API audiences. Passed directly to `WithAuthentication` in the handler chain.\n- **`Authorization AuthorizationInfo`** \u2014 holds the `Authorizer` and `RuleResolver`. Passed to `WithAuthorization`.\n- **`AdmissionControl admission.Interface`** \u2014 the composed admission chain. Set by calling `Plugins.NewFromPlugins` with the ordered list of enabled plugin names.\n- **`FlowControl utilflowcontrol.Interface`** \u2014 if non-nil, `WithPriorityAndFairness` is used; otherwise `WithMaxInFlightLimit` is used with `MaxRequestsInFlight` and `MaxMutatingRequestsInFlight`.\n- **`RequestTimeout time.Duration`** \u2014 the deadline applied to non-long-running requests by `WithRequestDeadline`. The APF work estimator uses `RequestTimeout/4` as its seat-hold timeout.\n- **`ShutdownDelayDuration time.Duration`** \u2014 how long the server continues serving after receiving a shutdown signal before stopping the listener. Defaults to 70 seconds. During this window `/readyz` returns failure but the server still processes requests, giving load balancers time to drain.\n- **`ShutdownSendRetryAfter bool`** \u2014 changes the shutdown mode. When true, after `ShutdownDelayDuration` the server keeps listening but returns HTTP 429 with `Retry-After: 1` and `Connection: close` for new requests, waiting until all in-flight non-long-running requests drain before stopping the listener with a 2-second hard timeout.\n- **`BuildHandlerChainFunc`** \u2014 defaults to `DefaultBuildHandlerChain`. Replacing this function is the primary way to customize the filter chain.\n- **`lifecycleSignals lifecycleSignals`** \u2014 private; holds the named channel-based signals that coordinate the shutdown sequence (see \u00a73.4).\n\n### 2.2 GenericAPIServer\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go`\n\n`GenericAPIServer` is the runtime server object. It is created by `Config.Complete().New(name, delegationTarget)`. Its most important fields:\n\n- **`Handler *APIServerHandler`** \u2014 the composed HTTP handler (see \u00a72.3).\n- **`delegationTarget DelegationTarget`** \u2014 the next server in the delegation chain. Requests that do not match any registered route fall through to this target's `UnprotectedHandler()`.\n- **`postStartHooks map[string]postStartHookEntry`** \u2014 hooks run after the HTTP server starts listening, before the server is considered ready.\n- **`preShutdownHooks map[string]preShutdownHookEntry`** \u2014 hooks run concurrently with the `ShutdownDelayDuration` sleep, before `NotAcceptingNewRequest` is signaled.\n- **`healthzChecks`, `livezChecks`, `readyzChecks`** \u2014 registered health checkers. `PrepareRun()` installs them at `/healthz`, `/livez`, and `/readyz` respectively.\n- **`lifecycleSignals`** \u2014 the set of named signals coordinating shutdown (see \u00a73.4).\n- **`ShutdownDelayDuration`**, **`ShutdownSendRetryAfter`**, **`ShutdownTimeout`** \u2014 copied from `Config`.\n\n`PrepareRun()` installs OpenAPI v2 and v3 specs, health endpoints, and a readiness shutdown check that starts failing `/readyz` as soon as `ShutdownInitiated` fires. It returns a `preparedGenericAPIServer` whose `RunWithContext(ctx)` method starts the HTTP server and the shutdown goroutine tree.\n\n### 2.3 APIServerHandler and the Director\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/handler.go`\n\n`APIServerHandler` holds four fields:\n\n```\nFullHandlerChain  http.Handler          // the complete filter chain; this is what net/http serves\nGoRestfulContainer *restful.Container   // go-restful routes for /api and /apis\nNonGoRestfulMux    *mux.PathRecorderMux // all other paths: /healthz, /metrics, /openapi, etc.\nDirector           http.Handler         // routes between the two above\n```\n\n`FullHandlerChain` is built by passing the `Director` through `Config.BuildHandlerChainFunc`. The `Director` inspects the request path against registered go-restful `WebService` root paths. If the path matches a registered API group prefix (e.g., `/apis/apps/v1/...`), the request is dispatched to `GoRestfulContainer`. Otherwise it falls through to `NonGoRestfulMux`.\n\nThe `/apis` path requires special handling: go-restful would 404 any path not exactly matching a registered route, but discovery requests to `/apis` and `/apis/` must be served. The `Director` handles this by checking for exact equality with `/apis` or `/apis/` before doing prefix matching.\n\n### 2.4 APIInstaller\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/installer.go`\n\n`APIInstaller` bridges the gap between a `rest.Storage` implementation and go-restful routes. Its `Install()` method iterates over the storage map in sorted order and calls `registerResourceHandlers` for each path.\n\n`registerResourceHandlers` performs type assertions against the storage object to discover which REST verbs it supports:\n\n```go\ncreater,    isCreater    := storage.(rest.Creater)\nlister,     isLister     := storage.(rest.Lister)\ngetter,     isGetter     := storage.(rest.Getter)\nupdater,    isUpdater    := storage.(rest.Updater)\npatcher,    isPatcher    := storage.(rest.Patcher)\nwatcher,    isWatcher    := storage.(rest.Watcher)\ngracefulDeleter, isGracefulDeleter := storage.(rest.GracefulDeleter)\nconnecter,  isConnecter  := storage.(rest.Connecter)\n```\n\nOnly the routes corresponding to implemented interfaces are registered. For namespace-scoped resources, routes are registered at both the namespaced path (`/apis/{group}/{version}/namespaces/{namespace}/{resource}`) and the cross-namespace path (`/apis/{group}/{version}/{resource}`). For cluster-scoped resources, only the non-namespaced path is registered.\n\nEach registered route is bound to a handler function from `pkg/endpoints/handlers/` (e.g., `GetResource`, `CreateResource`, `UpdateResource`, `PatchResource`, `DeleteResource`, `ListResource`, `WatchResource`). A `RequestScope` struct is constructed per resource and passed to each handler; it carries the serializer, convertor, authorizer, field manager, and resource/kind metadata needed to process requests without further lookups.\n\n### 2.5 REST Storage Interfaces\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/rest/rest.go`\n\nThe REST storage interface hierarchy defines the contract between `APIInstaller` and storage implementations:\n\n- **`Storage`** \u2014 base interface: `New() runtime.Object` and `Destroy()`. Every storage must implement this.\n- **`Getter`** \u2014 `Get(ctx, name, options) (runtime.Object, error)`\n- **`Lister`** \u2014 `NewList() runtime.Object` and `List(ctx, options) (runtime.Object, error)`\n- **`Creater`** \u2014 `New() runtime.Object` and `Create(ctx, obj, createValidation, options) (runtime.Object, error)`\n- **`NamedCreater`** \u2014 like `Creater` but also receives the client-provided name\n- **`Updater`** \u2014 `New() runtime.Object` and `Update(ctx, name, objInfo, createValidation, updateValidation, forceAllowCreate, options) (runtime.Object, bool, error)`\n- **`Patcher`** \u2014 composed of `Getter` + `Updater`; enables PATCH\n- **`GracefulDeleter`** \u2014 `Delete(ctx, name, deleteValidation, options) (runtime.Object, bool, error)`\n- **`CollectionDeleter`** \u2014 `DestroyFunc` for bulk delete\n- **`Watcher`** \u2014 `Watch(ctx, options) (watch.Interface, error)`\n- **`Connecter`** \u2014 `Connect(ctx, id, options, responder) (http.Handler, error)`; used for subresources like `exec`, `portforward`, `proxy`\n- **`StandardStorage`** \u2014 aggregates Getter, Lister, Creater, Updater, GracefulDeleter, Watcher, and Destroyer\n\nThe strategy interfaces (`RESTCreateStrategy`, `RESTUpdateStrategy`, `RESTDeleteStrategy`) are separate from the storage interfaces. They define resource-specific normalization and validation logic that the generic `Store` calls at the appropriate points in the CRUD lifecycle.\n\n`RESTCreateStrategy` requires:\n- `PrepareForCreate(ctx, obj)` \u2014 strips server-managed fields (e.g., status), normalizes the object\n- `Validate(ctx, obj) field.ErrorList` \u2014 structural validation\n- `Canonicalize(obj)` \u2014 final normalization before persistence\n\n`RESTUpdateStrategy` requires:\n- `PrepareForUpdate(ctx, obj, old)` \u2014 strips fields the client cannot set on update\n- `ValidateUpdate(ctx, obj, old) field.ErrorList`\n- `AllowCreateOnUpdate() bool` \u2014 whether PUT can create a non-existent object\n- `AllowUnconditionalUpdate() bool` \u2014 whether PUT without a `resourceVersion` is permitted\n\n### 2.6 Generic Registry Store\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go`\n\n`Store` is the canonical implementation of `StandardStorage`. It is parameterized by strategy objects and a `DryRunnableStorage` backend. Most built-in resource types embed or delegate to a `Store`.\n\n**Create path** (`store.create`):\n\n1. `rest.FillObjectMetaSystemFields` \u2014 sets `creationTimestamp`, generates a name from `generateName` if needed.\n2. `BeginCreate` hook (optional) \u2014 returns a commit/revert function called at the end of the operation.\n3. `rest.BeforeCreate(e.CreateStrategy, ctx, obj)` \u2014 calls `PrepareForCreate`, then `Validate`. Returns on first validation error.\n4. `createValidation(ctx, obj.DeepCopyObject())` \u2014 calls the admission chain's `Validate` phase (passed in as a closure from the endpoint handler).\n5. `e.Storage.Create(ctx, key, obj, out, ttl, dryRun)` \u2014 writes to the storage backend.\n6. `AfterCreate` hook (optional).\n7. `Decorator` (optional) \u2014 post-storage decoration, not persisted.\n\n**Update path** (`store.Update`):\n\nThe update is executed inside `e.Storage.GuaranteedUpdate`, which provides optimistic concurrency. The closure passed to `GuaranteedUpdate` receives the current object from storage and:\n\n1. Checks `existingResourceVersion`. If zero and `AllowCreateOnUpdate` is false, returns NotFound.\n2. Calls `objInfo.UpdatedObject(ctx, existing)` to merge the client's intent with the existing object (used by server-side apply and strategic merge patch).\n3. Validates the `resourceVersion` in the request against the stored version; returns a Conflict error if they differ (unless `AllowUnconditionalUpdate` is true).\n4. `BeginUpdate` hook (optional).\n5. `rest.BeforeUpdate(e.UpdateStrategy, ctx, obj, existing)` \u2014 calls `PrepareForUpdate`, then `ValidateUpdate`.\n6. `updateValidation(ctx, obj, existing)` \u2014 admission `Validate` phase.\n7. `ShouldDeleteDuringUpdate` check \u2014 if the object has no finalizers, has a `deletionTimestamp`, and `deletionGracePeriodSeconds` is zero, the update is converted to a delete.\n\n**Delete path** (`store.Delete`):\n\nDeletion is two-phase when finalizers are present. The first phase sets `deletionTimestamp` and `deletionGracePeriodSeconds` via `updateForGracefulDeletionAndFinalizers`, which itself calls `GuaranteedUpdate`. The second phase (immediate deletion) calls `e.Storage.Delete` only when all finalizers have been removed and the grace period has elapsed.\n\n### 2.7 Storage Interface and etcd3 Backend\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/interfaces.go`  \n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go`\n\n`storage.Interface` defines the contract between the generic registry and the storage backend:\n\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    Versioner() Versioner\n    Create(ctx, key string, obj, out runtime.Object, ttl uint64) error\n    Delete(ctx, key string, out runtime.Object, preconditions *Preconditions,\n           validateDeletion ValidateObjectFunc, cachedExistingObject runtime.Object,\n           opts DeleteOptions) error\n    Watch(ctx, key string, opts ListOptions) (watch.Interface, error)\n    Get(ctx, key string, opts GetOptions, objPtr runtime.Object) error\n    GetList(ctx, key string, opts ListOptions, listObj runtime.Object) error\n    GuaranteedUpdate(ctx, key string, destination runtime.Object, ignoreNotFound bool,\n                     preconditions *Preconditions, tryUpdate UpdateFunc,\n                     cachedExistingObject runtime.Object) error\n    ReadinessCheck() error\n    RequestWatchProgress(ctx) error\n    GetCurrentResourceVersion(ctx) (uint64, error)\n}\n```\n\nThe etcd3 `store` struct (`pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go`) implements this interface. Key behaviors:\n\n**`Create`**: Encodes the object with `runtime.Encode(s.codec, obj)`, then calls `s.transformer.TransformToStorage` (which applies encryption if configured), then issues an `OptimisticPut` with a precondition that the key must not exist (revision 0). If the key already exists, returns `storage.NewKeyExistsError`.\n\n**`GuaranteedUpdate`**: Implements a read-modify-write loop with compare-and-swap semantics:\n1. Reads the current state from etcd (or uses `cachedExistingObject` as a hint).\n2. Calls `preconditions.Check` to validate UID and resourceVersion preconditions.\n3. Calls `tryUpdate(existing, meta)` \u2014 the closure provided by the caller (e.g., `store.Update`'s inner function).\n4. Encodes the result and calls `s.transformer.TransformToStorage`.\n5. Issues `OptimisticPut(ctx, key, newData, origState.rev, PutOptions{GetOnFailure: true})` \u2014 an etcd transaction that succeeds only if the key's current revision matches `origState.rev`.\n6. If the transaction fails (another writer modified the key), fetches the new state and retries from step 2.\n7. If the encoded data is identical to the stored data and the stored data is not stale, skips the write entirely (no-op update optimization).\n\n**`TransformToStorage` / `TransformFromStorage`**: These calls on `value.Transformer` are the encryption boundary. For KMS v2, the transformer encrypts the serialized bytes with an AES-GCM DEK, prepends the encrypted DEK (itself encrypted by the KMS provider), and stores the result. On read, the DEK is decrypted (with caching) and used to decrypt the data.\n\n### 2.8 Watch Cache and Cacher\n\n**Files:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go`  \n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/watch_cache.go`\n\n`Cacher` wraps a `storage.Interface` and intercepts `Watch`, `Get`, and `GetList` calls to serve them from an in-memory cache, reducing load on etcd. It is the default storage layer used by the generic registry when `RESTOptionsGetter` is configured with caching enabled.\n\n**`watchCache`** maintains:\n- A `store.Indexer` holding the current state of all objects for the resource (used for List and point-in-time Get).\n- A ring buffer of `watchCacheEvent` entries representing recent mutations. The ring buffer starts at `defaultLowerBoundCapacity = 100` entries and grows up to `capacityUpperBound(eventFreshDuration)` (computed from `DefaultEventFreshDuration = 1m15s`). The upper bound is `defaultUpperBoundCapacity = 100 * 1024` entries.\n- A `sync.Cond` on which List calls wait when the requested `resourceVersion` is newer than the cache's current revision.\n\n**`Cacher`** maintains:\n- A `Reflector` that issues a single Watch against the underlying etcd3 store with `storageWatchListPageSize = 10000` and feeds events into `watchCache`.\n- `indexedWatchers` \u2014 a map from trigger field value to `[]*cacheWatcher`, plus an `allWatchers` list for watchers without a trigger. When an event arrives, the Cacher dispatches it to matching watchers by looking up the trigger value in the map and iterating `allWatchers`.\n- `bookmarkWatchers` \u2014 a time-bucketed set of watchers that need periodic bookmark events. Bookmarks are sent at `defaultBookmarkFrequency = 1 minute` intervals to allow clients to advance their `resourceVersion` without receiving object events.\n\n**Watch serving**: When a client calls `Cacher.Watch`, the Cacher:\n1. Checks cache readiness (returns 429 with `Retry-After` if not ready, under `ResilientWatchCacheInitialization`).\n2. Determines the `requiredResourceVersion` \u2014 the minimum cache revision the watch must be synchronized to before starting.\n3. Creates a `cacheWatcher` with a buffered channel sized by `suggestedWatchChannelSize`.\n4. Calls `waitUntilWatchCacheFreshAndForceAllEvents` to block until the cache is at least at `requiredResourceVersion`.\n5. Replays historical events from the ring buffer that the client missed, then switches to live dispatch.\n\n**List serving**: `Cacher.GetList` serves from the `store.Indexer` snapshot when the requested `resourceVersion` is satisfiable from cache. If the requested version is newer than the cache, it waits on the `sync.Cond`. If the version is too old (older than the oldest event in the ring buffer), it falls through to etcd.\n\n### 2.9 Admission\n\n**Files:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/interfaces.go`  \n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/chain.go`  \n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugins.go`\n\nAdmission is a two-phase pipeline. The `admission.Interface` hierarchy:\n\n- **`MutationInterface`** \u2014 `Admit(ctx, Attributes, ObjectInterfaces) error`. Called first; plugins may mutate the object.\n- **`ValidationInterface`** \u2014 `Validate(ctx, Attributes, ObjectInterfaces) error`. Called second; plugins must not mutate.\n\n`chainAdmissionHandler` (a `[]Interface`) implements both phases by iterating the slice. For each handler, it first checks `handler.Handles(operation)` \u2014 if false, the handler is skipped entirely. For the mutation phase, it type-asserts to `MutationInterface` and calls `Admit`; for validation, it type-asserts to `ValidationInterface` and calls `Validate`. The chain returns on the first error.\n\n`Plugins.Register(name, factory)` registers a plugin factory by name at init time. `Plugins.NewFromPlugins(pluginNames, configProvider, initializer, decorator)` instantiates plugins in the specified order, calls `initializer.Initialize(plugin)` on each (which injects informers, clients, and other dependencies), and wraps the result in a `chainAdmissionHandler`.\n\n`Attributes` carries the full request context to each plugin: the object, old object, operation type, resource/subresource GVR, user info, dry-run flag, and a mutable annotation map that is written to the audit log.\n\nThe `reinvocation` mechanism (used by mutating admission webhooks) allows a plugin to signal that it modified the object and requests that earlier plugins be re-run. The `ReinvocationContext` tracks this state across the chain.\n\n### 2.10 API Priority and Fairness\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go`\n\nWhen `Config.FlowControl` is non-nil, `WithPriorityAndFairness` replaces the simpler `WithMaxInFlightLimit`. The APF controller:\n\n1. Watches `FlowSchema` and `PriorityLevelConfiguration` objects via informers.\n2. On any change, re-reads all config objects and rebuilds the internal dispatch table.\n3. Classifies each incoming request by matching it against `FlowSchema` rules (in priority order) to determine its `PriorityLevel` and `FlowDistinguisher`.\n4. Enqueues the request in the appropriate virtual queue. If the queue is full, the request is rejected with HTTP 429.\n5. Dispatches requests from queues using a weighted fair queuing algorithm, respecting the `nominalConcurrencyShares` of each priority level.\n\nBorrowing between priority levels is adjusted every `borrowingAdjustmentPeriod = 10 seconds`. The adjustment uses smoothed seat demand figures with a decay coefficient of `seatDemandSmoothingCoefficient = 0.977` (half-life \u2248 5 minutes).\n\nThe work estimator computes the \"width\" (seat count) of a request based on the number of objects in storage for the resource (`StorageObjectCountTracker`) and the estimated response size. The maximum seats a single request can claim from a priority level is `priorityLevelMaxSeatsPercent = 15%` of the nominal concurrency limit.\n\n### 2.11 KMS v2 Envelope Encryption\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/value/encrypt/envelope/kmsv2/envelope.go`\n\n`envelopeTransformer` implements `value.Transformer` using a KEK-DEK (Key Encryption Key / Data Encryption Key) scheme:\n\n- **Write path** (`TransformToStorage`): Calls `stateFunc()` to get the current KMS state (which includes the current encrypted DEK source and key ID). Encrypts the plaintext data with an AES-GCM DEK derived from the state. Serializes the result as an `EncryptedObject` protobuf containing the encrypted data, the encrypted DEK source, the key ID, and annotations.\n- **Read path** (`TransformFromStorage`): Deserializes the `EncryptedObject`. Looks up the DEK in an LRU cache keyed by `generateCacheKey(encryptedDEKSourceType, encryptedDEKSource, keyID, annotations)`. On a cache miss, calls `envelopeService.Decrypt` (a gRPC call to the KMS plugin) to recover the DEK, then caches it. Decrypts the data with the recovered DEK.\n- **Staleness**: A read result is marked stale if the stored key ID differs from the current write key ID. Stale objects are re-encrypted on the next write, enabling key rotation without a migration job.\n\nThe `encryptedDEKSourceMaxSize = 1 KB` limit bounds the size of the encrypted DEK source stored alongside each object.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Server Chain Assembly\n\n**File:** `cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go:CreateServerChain`\n\nThe three servers are assembled in delegation order, innermost first:\n\n```\nnotFoundHandler\n    \u2191 delegates to\napiExtensionsServer  (CRD server; handles /apis/apiextensions.k8s.io/...)\n    \u2191 delegates to\nkubeAPIServer        (core + named groups; handles /api/v1/..., /apis/apps/..., etc.)\n    \u2191 delegates to\naggregatorServer     (outermost; handles /apis/<extension-group>/..., proxies to extension API servers)\n```\n\nEach server's `Handler.NonGoRestfulMux` has the next server's `UnprotectedHandler()` as its not-found handler. A request that does not match any route in the aggregator falls through to kubeAPIServer, then to apiExtensionsServer, and finally to the `notFoundHandler` which returns a structured 404.\n\nThe entry point is:\n```\nRun() \u2192 CreateServerChain() \u2192 aggregatorServer.GenericAPIServer.PrepareRun() \u2192 prepared.RunWithContext(ctx)\n```\n\n### 3.2 Filter Chain Execution Order\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go:DefaultBuildHandlerChain`\n\n`DefaultBuildHandlerChain` wraps the `Director` in a sequence of `http.Handler` decorators. Because each decorator wraps the previous one, the last decorator applied is the outermost (first to execute). The execution order for an incoming request is:\n\n| Order | Handler | Purpose |\n|---|---|---|\n| 1 | `WithAuditInit` | Initializes the audit event context; must be outermost so all subsequent handlers can annotate it |\n| 2 | `WithPanicRecovery` | Catches panics in all downstream handlers; logs stack trace and returns 500 |\n| 3 | `WithMuxAndDiscoveryComplete` | Returns 503 until all API groups are registered and discovery is complete |\n| 4 | `WithRequestReceivedTimestamp` | Records the wall-clock time the request arrived |\n| 5 | `WithRequestInfo` | Parses the URL into a `RequestInfo` (verb, resource, namespace, name, subresource) and stores it in context |\n| 6 | `WithRoutine` *(optional)* | Moves downstream handler execution to a new goroutine to reduce stack depth; enabled by `APIServingWithRoutine` feature gate |\n| 7 | `WithLatencyTrackers` | Attaches latency tracking state to context for SLI metrics |\n| 8 | `WithHTTPLogging` | Logs the request/response after completion |\n| 9 | `WithRetryAfter` *(if ShutdownSendRetryAfter)* | Returns 429 + `Retry-After: 1` + `Connection: close` once `NotAcceptingNewRequest` is signaled |\n| 10 | `WithHSTS` | Adds `Strict-Transport-Security` header if configured |\n| 11 | `WithCacheControl` | Adds `Cache-Control: no-cache, private` to prevent proxy caching of API responses |\n| 12 | `WithProbabilisticGoaway` *(optional)* | Sends HTTP/2 GOAWAY at configured probability; enabled when `GoawayChance > 0` |\n| 13 | `WithWatchTerminationDuringShutdown` *(optional)* | Tracks active watch requests in `WatchRequestWaitGroup`; enabled when `ShutdownWatchTerminationGracePeriod > 0` |\n| 14 | `WithWaitGroup` | Tracks non-long-running requests in `NonLongRunningRequestWaitGroup` for drain accounting |\n| 15 | `WithRequestDeadline` | Sets a context deadline from the `timeout` query parameter, bounded by `Config.RequestTimeout` |\n| 16 | `WithTimeoutForNonLongRunningRequests` | Enforces the deadline by running the downstream handler in a goroutine; returns 504 if the deadline fires first |\n| 17 | `WithWarningRecorder` | Attaches a `WarningRecorder` to context; downstream handlers call `warning.AddWarning` to emit `Warning:` response headers |\n| 18 | `WithCORS` | Handles CORS preflight and adds CORS headers for configured origins |\n| 19 | `WithAuthentication` | Runs the authenticator chain; on failure, calls the `failedHandler` (which logs an audit event and returns 401) |\n| 20 | `WithTracing` *(optional)* | Starts an OpenTelemetry span; placed after authentication so authenticated identity is available for sampling decisions |\n| 21 | `WithAudit` | Attaches the audit policy evaluator; writes the audit event on response completion |\n| 22 | `WithImpersonation` / `WithConstrainedImpersonation` | Processes `Impersonate-*` headers; re-authorizes the impersonation request |\n| 23 | `WithPriorityAndFairness` / `WithMaxInFlightLimit` | Enforces concurrency limits; may queue or reject the request |\n| 24 | `WithAuthorization` | Calls the authorizer; returns 403 on denial |\n| 25 | `apiHandler` (Director) | Routes to `GoRestfulContainer` or `NonGoRestfulMux` |\n\n### 3.3 Request Processing: CREATE Example\n\nAfter the filter chain, a `POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/deployments` request reaches the go-restful route registered by `APIInstaller`. The bound handler is `CreateResource(r rest.Creater, scope *RequestScope, admit admission.Interface)`.\n\n**`createHandler`** (`pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go`):\n\n1. Extracts namespace and name from the URL via `scope.Namer.Name(req)`.\n2. Applies a hard timeout of `requestTimeoutUpperBound = 34 seconds` via `context.WithTimeout`, independent of the `WithRequestDeadline` timeout set by the filter chain. The effective deadline is the minimum of the two.\n3. Negotiates the output media type (`NegotiateOutputMediaType`) and input serializer (`NegotiateInputSerializer`).\n4. Reads and size-limits the request body (`limitedReadBodyWithRecordMetric`).\n5. Decodes the body into an internal-version object using `scope.Serializer.DecoderToVersion`. If `FieldValidation` is `Warn` or `Strict`, uses the strict decoder.\n6. Validates the API version in the decoded object matches the request URL's group/version.\n7. Wipes server-managed `ObjectMeta` fields (`WipeObjectMetaSystemFields`) to prevent clients from setting `uid`, `resourceVersion`, `creationTimestamp`, etc.\n8. Constructs `admissionAttributes` with the object, operation, resource, user info, and dry-run flag.\n9. Calls `scope.FieldManager.UpdateNoErrors` to apply server-side apply field ownership tracking.\n10. Calls `mutatingAdmission.Admit(ctx, admissionAttributes, scope)` \u2014 the mutation phase of the admission chain.\n11. Calls `r.Create(ctx, name, obj, rest.AdmissionToValidateObjectFunc(admit, admissionAttributes, scope), options)` \u2014 this is the `Store.create` method, which runs the validation admission phase internally.\n12. If the object is too large after field manager metadata is added, retries after stripping `managedFields`.\n13. Serializes the result with `transformResponseObject` and writes HTTP 201.\n\n**`Store.create`** (`pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go`):\n\n1. `BeginCreate` hook.\n2. `rest.BeforeCreate` \u2014 `PrepareForCreate` + `Validate`.\n3. `createValidation` \u2014 admission `Validate` phase (the closure from step 11 above).\n4. `e.Storage.Create` \u2014 writes to the Cacher (which writes to etcd3).\n\n**etcd3 `store.Create`** (`pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go`):\n\n1. `runtime.Encode(s.codec, obj)` \u2014 serializes to the storage version (e.g., `apps/v1`).\n2. `s.transformer.TransformToStorage` \u2014 encrypts if KMS is configured.\n3. `s.client.Kubernetes.OptimisticPut(ctx, key, data, 0, ...)` \u2014 etcd transaction with `version == 0` precondition (key must not exist).\n4. Decodes the stored bytes back into `out` using the etcd revision as the `resourceVersion`.\n\n### 3.4 Shutdown Lifecycle\n\n**Files:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go:RunWithContext`  \n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/lifecycle_signals.go`\n\nThe shutdown sequence is coordinated by named channel-based signals. The `RunWithContext` goroutine tree:\n\n```\nctx cancelled (SIGTERM received)\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500\u25ba ShutdownInitiated.Signal()\n    \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u25ba /readyz starts returning failure\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500\u25ba sleep(ShutdownDelayDuration = 70s)\n    \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u25ba AfterShutdownDelayDuration.Signal()\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500\u25ba PreShutdownHooks run concurrently\n            \u2514\u2500\u25ba PreShutdownHooksStopped.Signal()\n\nAfterShutdownDelayDuration + PreShutdownHooksStopped\n    \u2514\u2500\u25ba NotAcceptingNewRequest.Signal()\n\n[ShutdownSendRetryAfter = false]:\n    NotAcceptingNewRequest\n        \u2514\u2500\u25ba stopHTTPServerCtx cancelled\n                \u2514\u2500\u25ba net/http Server.Shutdown(60s timeout)\n                        \u2514\u2500\u25ba HTTPServerStoppedListening.Signal()\n                        \u2514\u2500\u25ba InFlightRequestsDrained.Signal() (after NonLongRunning + Watch WaitGroups drain)\n\n[ShutdownSendRetryAfter = true]:\n    NotAcceptingNewRequest\n        \u2514\u2500\u25ba WithRetryAfter returns 429 for new requests\n        \u2514\u2500\u25ba wait for NonLongRunningRequestWaitGroup + WatchRequestWaitGroup to drain\n                \u2514\u2500\u25ba InFlightRequestsDrained.Signal()\n                        \u2514\u2500\u25ba stopHTTPServerCtx cancelled\n                                \u2514\u2500\u25ba net/http Server.Shutdown(2s timeout)\n                                        \u2514\u2500\u25ba HTTPServerStoppedListening.Signal()\n```\n\nThe audit backend's `Shutdown()` is called after `InFlightRequestsDrained`, ensuring all in-flight request audit events are flushed before the backend closes.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes and Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 etcd Unavailability\n\nWhen etcd is unreachable, `storage.Interface` operations return errors that propagate as HTTP 500 or 503 responses. The Cacher continues to serve Watch and List from its in-memory state, but the served data may be stale. The staleness bound is the age of the last successfully processed etcd event.\n\nWrites (Create, Update, Delete) always go through to etcd and will fail immediately if etcd is unavailable. There is no write buffering or retry at the storage layer; callers receive the error and must retry.\n\nThe `ReadinessCheck()` method on `storage.Interface` is called by the storage readiness hook (`pkg/server/storage_readiness_hook.go`), which blocks `/readyz` until all registered storage backends report ready. This prevents the server from receiving traffic before its storage is accessible.\n\n### 4.2 Watch Cache Initialization\n\nOn startup, the Cacher issues a `List` followed by a `Watch` against etcd to populate the `watchCache`. Until this initial sync completes, the cache is not ready. Under `ResilientWatchCacheInitialization` (feature gate), `Cacher.Watch` returns HTTP 429 with a `Retry-After` header computed from the estimated remaining initialization time, rather than blocking indefinitely. Under the old behavior, `Watch` blocks until the cache is ready or the context is cancelled.\n\nIf the watch cache falls behind etcd (e.g., due to a slow event processing loop), the ring buffer may overflow. When a client requests a `resourceVersion` older than the oldest event in the ring buffer, the Cacher cannot serve the watch from cache and must fall through to etcd, which issues a new `Watch` from that revision. This is transparent to the client but increases etcd load.\n\n### 4.3 Optimistic Concurrency Conflicts\n\n`GuaranteedUpdate` retries on etcd CAS failures. Each retry re-reads the current state from etcd and re-applies the `tryUpdate` closure. This means the closure must be idempotent with respect to the object's current state. If many writers contend on the same key, the retry loop can execute many times. There is no backoff; retries are immediate. High contention on a single object (e.g., a heavily annotated ConfigMap used as a lock) can cause significant CPU and etcd load.\n\nThe `OptimisticLockErrorMsg` (\"the object has been modified; please apply your changes to the latest version and try again\") is returned to the client as HTTP 409 Conflict when the `resourceVersion` in the request does not match the stored version. This is the expected signal for clients to re-fetch and retry.\n\n### 4.4 Admission Chain Failures\n\nThe admission chain returns on the first error from any plugin. A misbehaving or slow admission webhook can block all mutating or validating requests for the affected resources. The `WithTimeoutForNonLongRunningRequests` filter enforces a deadline on the entire request, including admission, so a hung webhook will eventually cause a 504 response rather than blocking indefinitely.\n\nDry-run requests (`?dryRun=All`) pass through the full admission chain (including webhooks) but do not write to storage. Admission plugins that have side effects must check `Attributes.IsDryRun()` and skip those side effects.\n\n### 4.5 Handler Chain Timeout Layering\n\nThere are three independent timeout mechanisms that interact:\n\n1. **`WithRequestDeadline`** \u2014 sets a context deadline from the `timeout` query parameter, bounded by `Config.RequestTimeout`. This is the primary mechanism for client-specified timeouts.\n2. **`WithTimeoutForNonLongRunningRequests`** \u2014 enforces the deadline by running the downstream handler in a goroutine and returning 504 if the deadline fires. The goroutine continues running after the 504 is sent, which means the storage write may still complete even after the client receives a timeout.\n3. **`requestTimeoutUpperBound = 34 seconds`** \u2014 a hard cap applied inside `createHandler`, `deleteHandler`, and `patchHandler` via `context.WithTimeout`. This is independent of the filter chain deadline and ensures that even if `Config.RequestTimeout` is very large, individual write handlers have a bounded execution time.\n\nLong-running requests (watches, `exec`, `portforward`, `proxy`) are exempt from `WithTimeoutForNonLongRunningRequests`. They are identified by `Config.LongRunningFunc` and tracked separately in `WatchRequestWaitGroup`.\n\n### 4.6 Watch Channel Backpressure\n\nEach `cacheWatcher` has a bounded channel. If a watcher's consumer is slow and the channel fills, the Cacher's event dispatch loop will block on that watcher's channel send. To prevent a slow watcher from blocking all other watchers, the Cacher uses a non-blocking send with a fallback: if the channel is full, the watcher is terminated and the client receives a watch error, forcing it to re-list and re-watch. The channel size is computed by `suggestedWatchChannelSize` based on whether an indexed trigger is in use.\n\n### 4.7 JSON Patch Operation Limit\n\n`PatchResource` (`pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`) enforces `maxJSONPatchOperations = 10000` for JSON Patch (`application/json-patch+json`) requests. Requests exceeding this limit are rejected with HTTP 422. This prevents denial-of-service via pathologically large patch documents.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points\n\n### 5.1 Custom Handler Chain\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go`\n\n`Config.BuildHandlerChainFunc` defaults to `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` but can be replaced entirely:\n\n```go\nconfig.BuildHandlerChainFunc = func(apiHandler http.Handler, c *server.Config) http.Handler {\n    handler := server.DefaultBuildHandlerChain(apiHandler, c)\n    handler = myCustomFilter(handler)\n    return handler\n}\n```\n\nReplacing `BuildHandlerChainFunc` gives full control over the filter chain. Wrapping `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` is the safer approach for adding filters without disrupting the existing chain.\n\nIndividual filters can also be added to `NonGoRestfulMux` for non-API paths (metrics, health, debug endpoints) without touching the API handler chain.\n\n### 5.2 Custom REST Storage\n\nTo add a new resource, implement the appropriate subset of the REST storage interfaces from `pkg/registry/rest/rest.go`. The minimum is `Storage` (for the resource to appear in discovery) plus whichever verb interfaces correspond to the desired HTTP methods.\n\nFor resources that need standard CRUD semantics backed by etcd, embed `registry.Store` and supply:\n- `NewFunc` and `NewListFunc` \u2014 constructors for the resource and list types\n- `KeyRootFunc` and `KeyFunc` \u2014 etcd key path constructors\n- `CreateStrategy`, `UpdateStrategy`, `DeleteStrategy` \u2014 resource-specific normalization and validation\n- `PredicateFunc` \u2014 field selector to storage predicate translation\n\nRegister the storage with `GenericAPIServer.InstallAPIGroups` or `InstallLegacyAPIGroup`, which calls `APIInstaller.Install()` to register the go-restful routes.\n\n### 5.3 Admission Plugins\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugins.go`\n\nRegister a plugin at init time:\n\n```go\nfunc init() {\n    admission.RegisterPlugin(\"MyPlugin\", func(config io.Reader) (admission.Interface, error) {\n        return NewMyPlugin(config)\n    })\n}\n```\n\nThe plugin struct implements `MutationInterface`, `ValidationInterface`, or both. It also implements `admission.InitializationValidator` if it needs to validate its own initialization, and `genericadmissioninitializer.WantsExternalKubeClientSet` (or similar initializer interfaces) to receive injected dependencies.\n\nThe plugin is activated by including its name in the `--enable-admission-plugins` flag. The order in the flag determines the order in the chain.\n\n### 5.4 Post-Start and Pre-Shutdown Hooks\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/hooks.go`\n\n```go\nserver.AddPostStartHook(\"my-controller\", func(ctx server.PostStartHookContext) error {\n    go myController.Run(ctx.Context)\n    return nil\n})\n\nserver.AddPreShutdownHook(\"my-cleanup\", func() error {\n    return myController.Cleanup()\n})\n```\n\n`PostStartHookFunc` receives a `PostStartHookContext` with a `LoopbackClientConfig` (a privileged in-process client) and a `context.Context` that is cancelled when the server stops. The hook must return promptly; long-running work should be started in a goroutine. The server's `/readyz` endpoint does not become ready until all post-start hooks have returned.\n\n`PreShutdownHookFunc` runs concurrently with the `ShutdownDelayDuration` sleep. The `NotAcceptingNewRequest` signal is not fired until both `AfterShutdownDelayDuration` and `PreShutdownHooksStopped` have fired, so pre-shutdown hooks have the full `ShutdownDelayDuration` window to complete cleanup that requires API access.\n\n### 5.5 Health Checks\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/healthz.go`\n\n```go\nserver.AddHealthChecks(healthz.NamedCheck(\"my-dependency\", func(r *http.Request) error {\n    if !myDependency.IsHealthy() {\n        return fmt.Errorf(\"my-dependency is not healthy\")\n    }\n    return nil\n}))\n```\n\n`AddHealthChecks` adds to all three endpoints (`/healthz`, `/livez`, `/readyz`). `AddReadyzChecks` adds only to `/readyz`. The distinction matters: `/livez` failures cause the process to be restarted by the kubelet; `/readyz` failures cause the load balancer to stop sending traffic.\n\n### 5.6 Storage Transformers (Encryption)\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/value/`\n\n`Config.ResourceTransformers` accepts a `storagevalue.ResourceTransformers` implementation that maps `schema.GroupResource` to `value.Transformer`. The etcd3 store calls `transformer.TransformToStorage` on write and `transformer.TransformFromStorage` on read.\n\nTo add a custom encryption scheme, implement `value.Transformer`:\n\n```go\ntype Transformer interface {\n    TransformFromStorage(ctx context.Context, data []byte, dataCtx Context) (out []byte, stale bool, err error)\n    TransformToStorage(ctx context.Context, data []byte, dataCtx Context) (out []byte, err error)\n}\n```\n\nThe `stale` return value from `TransformFromStorage` signals that the stored data should be re-encrypted on the next write (used for key rotation).\n\n### 5.7 Custom Storage Backend\n\n`storage.Interface` can be implemented to replace etcd entirely. The implementation must provide correct `Versioner` semantics (monotonically increasing resource versions), atomic `GuaranteedUpdate` with compare-and-swap, and a `Watch` that delivers ordered events with no gaps. The `Cacher` wraps any `storage.Interface`, so a custom backend automatically gets the watch cache layer.\n\n### 5.8 Feature Gates\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/features/`\n\nSeveral behaviors in the library are gated by feature flags accessible via `Config.FeatureGate`:\n\n- `APIServerTracing` \u2014 enables `WithTracing` in the handler chain\n- `APIServingWithRoutine` \u2014 enables `WithRoutine` to reduce goroutine stack depth\n- `ConstrainedImpersonation` \u2014 uses `WithConstrainedImpersonation` instead of `WithImpersonation`\n- `ResilientWatchCacheInitialization` \u2014 returns 429 instead of blocking on unready cache\n- `StorageVersionHash` \u2014 includes storage version hash in discovery documents\n- `StorageVersionAPI` \u2014 enables the `StorageVersion` API for storage migration tracking\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### Startup Sequencing\n\nThe server does not become ready (`/readyz` returns 200) until:\n1. All post-start hooks have returned successfully.\n2. All registered storage backends pass `ReadinessCheck()`.\n3. The `MuxAndDiscoveryComplete` signal fires (all API groups registered and discovery populated).\n4. `ShutdownInitiated` has not fired.\n\nThe `StorageInitializationTimeout` field in `Config` sets the maximum time to wait for storage readiness before declaring the server unhealthy. The `LivezGracePeriod` field allows `/livez` to return success for a configurable window after startup even if post-start hooks have not completed, preventing premature restarts during slow initialization.\n\n### Graceful Shutdown Tuning\n\nThe two shutdown modes have different operational characteristics:\n\n**`ShutdownSendRetryAfter = false`** (default): The server stops accepting new TCP connections at `T0 + ShutdownDelayDuration`. Existing connections are drained for up to `ShutdownTimeout = 60s`. This is simpler but means clients on existing connections may receive errors if they send new requests after `T0 + ShutdownDelayDuration`.\n\n**`ShutdownSendRetryAfter = true`**: The server keeps accepting connections but returns 429 for new requests after `T0 + ShutdownDelayDuration`. This is more client-friendly (clients can retry immediately) but requires that clients respect the `Retry-After` header. The listener stops only after all in-flight requests drain, with a 2-second hard stop. This mode is appropriate when clients are known to reuse connections aggressively.\n\n`ShutdownDelayDuration = 70s` is chosen to exceed the typical endpoint propagation time in a Kubernetes cluster (the time for a load balancer to detect `/readyz` failure and stop routing traffic). Reducing this value risks sending requests to a server that is about to stop.\n\n### Watch Cache Sizing\n\nThe watch cache ring buffer grows dynamically between `defaultLowerBoundCapacity = 100` and `defaultUpperBoundCapacity = 100 * 1024` events. The upper bound is also constrained by `capacityUpperBound(DefaultEventFreshDuration)`, which computes the maximum number of events that could arrive in `DefaultEventFreshDuration = 1m15s` at the observed event rate.\n\nA small ring buffer increases the probability that a slow watcher will fall behind the buffer and be forced to re-list. A large ring buffer consumes more memory. The buffer size is per resource type, so a cluster with many resource types and high churn can accumulate significant memory in watch caches.\n\n### APF Configuration\n\nThe APF controller reads `FlowSchema` and `PriorityLevelConfiguration` objects from the API server itself. During startup, before these objects are available, the controller uses bootstrap defaults (`pkg/apis/flowcontrol/bootstrap/`). Misconfigured APF objects (e.g., a `FlowSchema` that matches all requests with a very low priority level) can cause legitimate requests to be queued or rejected. The `borrowingAdjustmentPeriod = 10s` means that a sudden burst of requests may take up to 10 seconds for the borrowing mechanism to adapt.\n\n### Audit Log Volume\n\n`WithAudit` writes an audit event for every request that passes authentication. The audit policy (`AuditPolicyRuleEvaluator`) controls which requests are logged and at what level (None, Metadata, Request, RequestResponse). `RequestResponse` level captures full request and response bodies, which can generate very large audit events for List responses. Admission plugins can add annotations to audit events via `Attributes.AddAnnotation`, which are included in the audit log at the configured level.\n\n### Encryption Key Rotation\n\nKMS v2 key rotation is online: the new key ID is reflected in `stateFunc()`, and subsequent writes use the new DEK. Existing objects are re-encrypted lazily on the next write. To force re-encryption of all objects (e.g., after revoking an old key), a storage migration must be triggered. The `StorageVersionAPI` feature gate and `StorageVersion` objects track which objects have been migrated to the current storage version, and the same mechanism can be used to track encryption migration.\n\n---\n\n## 7.
